---

> **[THIS TABLE — C1 OUTCOME — 2026-05-24]**
>
> **Geometry broken at the ranch.** The opening diagram at the estancia was disrupted by the players. Cattle and swarm fell. The Luz Mala descended. Don Eusebio watched from the ridge and knows — the investigators tore apart part of his opening. He attempted to redraw the blood arcs before C4. The pit's geometry is degraded, not closed. The entity noticed the disruption; it is why it has been working from below ever since.
>
> **Concepción — DEAD.** The campaign assumes she survives C1. At this table, she did not.
>
> Downstream consequences:
> - Don Eusebio's C7 confession is grimmer. He sent her away injured, and she didn't make it. He volunteered her. He knows it. He will stand in the outer ring in C8 without being asked — he has nothing left to lose. His motivation is not redemption. It's settlement.
> - The quiet victory callback in C9 (*"se quedó callada de golpe"* at her cousin's house in Azul) is gone.
> - Any investigator who failed to save her carries that weight. Don Eusebio knows who was there.

---

# CHAPTER 2 — LAS SEÑALES → LA CAPILLA
### *The Signs → The Chapel*

**Arc Goal**: Break the false premise → show the counter-ritual → tragedy (La Llorona)
**Emotional Arc**: Doubt → Disquiet → Grief
**Key Seed**: Not all rituals are the same. Someone was trying to stop this.

---

## OPENING SITUATION

The investigators have returned from the south pasture with questions Don Eusebio cannot answer — because Don Eusebio is not at the estancia. He rode east sometime during the afternoon, leaving an unfinished letter to a "Don A. Quirce" in Buenos Aires, and his only foreman, Tomás, is as surprised and angry as the investigators are. The tracks do not match any indigenous raiding pattern. The geometry is too precise. The patrón ran. Something doesn't fit, and the man who might explain it has fled in the same direction the old trail leads.

This chapter begins with the investigators following that trail — the patrón's fresh hoofprints overlaid on older, stranger tracks from the pit's eastern rim — east, toward a place the foreman called *San Ruiz*. The trail leads to a burned chapel, and to a ghost who has been waiting for someone to listen.

**Standard path — follow the trail east**: Don Eusebio's palomino is recently shod and leaves a clean canter pattern. An investigator with **Tracking** can follow without difficulty for the first few hours; the trail veers north-east at the forked creek, though — Don Eusebio is heading toward the ridge above the tribal encampment (the site of C3), not San Ruiz. The *older* trail, the one the investigators have been drawn to since the pit, continues straight east. This is the choice point: follow the patrón (→ skip to a pre-San Ruiz glimpse of Don Eusebio at the ridge, then return to San Ruiz in C3) or follow the older geometry-trail (→ standard entry into San Ruiz below). Either choice converges on the same plot. Let players pick. If they follow Don Eusebio, they will lose him at the ridge — he slipped them, because he knows the land — but they will see him from a distance, dismounted, watching the tribal camp through a spyglass. This sighting alone reframes him and seeds C3.

**If investigators refuse to go east and try to wait at the estancia**: Tomás, shaken and without leadership, will press them to *do something* — he offers horses and his personal guidance (though he will not enter the pit again, and is uncomfortable leaving Concepción unattended). If players are still passive, a rural-police runner arrives the next morning with a report: *"Han visto luces raras sobre el campanario viejo de San Ruiz, tres noches seguidas. Desapareció una persona del rancho de afuera más cercano. El comisario solicita el parecer de ustedes, en su carácter de investigadores autorizados en el lugar."* — *"Strange lights seen over the old bell tower of San Ruiz, three nights running. One person has disappeared from the nearest outlying rancho. The police chief requests your opinion as the qualified investigators on site."* This is the hard pull east.

**If investigators first return to Don Eusebio's study and force the lock**: The door has a heavy iron lock (STR roll or Locksmith). Breaking it early — before the players have the context of C3 — will give them access to the manuscript early, but they will not have the Mapudungun chants needed to read it safely. See **Alternate Path: Early Manuscript** in the GM Notes at the end of this chapter.

**If investigators track the old (non-Eusebio) eastern trail**: The tracks from the pit's eastern rim are old but present. They follow the pattern — looping, stopping, restarting — but always trending east. Eventually the ground changes: harder, caliche-rich. The tracks become intermittent. Then: a road. The road leads to San Ruiz.

---

## THE WORLD: SAN RUIZ

**Setting**: San Ruiz is — was — a small farming settlement, perhaps forty years old. Founded by a mix of Criollo settlers and converted Tehuelche families who came in under the missions, it had perhaps twelve households at its peak. Adobe houses, a communal well, an orchard of peach trees now wild and leggy, a small chapel on the east end of the settlement.

> *El pueblo está quieto. No quieto-de-abandonado, no quieto-de-pueblo-fantasma — algo intermedio. Las casas están enteras. Las puertas, abiertas. Hay pan sobre una mesa adentro de una ventana, duro como piedra. Ropa tendida en una soga, descolorida hasta el gris. El durazno crece sin freno sobre el camino. No huele a podredumbre. No hay cuerpos. No hay huesos en la calle. Apenas — un lugar al que la gente se fue rápido, mientras estaba usando las cosas.*

> *En el centro de la plaza del pueblo hay un brocal de piedra — la boca tendrá vara y media de ancho. Cuando ustedes pasan al lado a caballo, un sonido: un balido suave, después silencio. **Hay una cabra adentro del aljibe.** Una cabra marrón con blanco, viva, parada en una repisa de mampostería caída unas tres varas más abajo. Está ilesa. No tiene soga. El aljibe está seco — no hay agua en el fondo, sólo piedras y la cabra. Los mira desde abajo sin alarma. No vuelve a balar.* (GM-only — do not read: investigators who try to fetch her up will find she does not resist being lifted, but the moment her hooves touch grass she walks back to the well and jumps in. She has done this before. Whoever once tried to rescue her gave up. **Do not name this. Do not explain it. The goat lives in the well.**)

> **Atmospheric runner — the goat (D5/3a)**: This is one of the campaign's three quiet recurring motifs (see `flowmap.md`). The goat is *still alive throughout the campaign*. She does not eat (Spot Hidden in C2 will find no goat-droppings near her ledge). She does not appear to bleed if cut. She watches. She is not malevolent and she is not friendly. **No NPC ever brings her up directly.** Rosa, asked about her, will say only *"Está ahí desde antes de que se fueran. Yo le tiro pasto a veces. No le hace falta."* — *"She has been there since before they left. I throw her grass sometimes. She doesn't need it."* If players return to San Ruiz at any later point in the campaign — C8 if they pass through on the ride east, the C12 epilogue — **the goat is still there.** This is the campaign's most patient witness. She is not a clue. She is the campaign reminding the players that what is happening in the geometry leaks into the ordinary.
>
> *Una cabra vive en el brocal del aljibe comunal. Los mira con pupilas horizontales y mastica.*

> **[THIS TABLE — 2026-05-24] ALTERNATE OUTCOME — GOAT EXTRACTED.** The players successfully extracted the goat from the well (two injuries). She did not walk back in. The well is now empty. Rosa's *"la cabra está ahí"* was her reading a fixed point in the geometry — present tense, always, like naming the church on the square. The investigators removed the last constant in her reading of San Ruiz. The goat now follows the party. She watches the gravely injured PC. She is likely a Pombero marker. **When players return to San Ruiz, the well is empty.** Full implications: `TABLE-STATE.md` — The Goat Thread.

**Keeper Notes**:
- San Ruiz was evacuated approximately 14 months ago. The departure was orderly enough to take people and animals but not belongings. They left mid-meal, mid-task.
  - **Timeline clarification** (Keeper): The evacuation pre-dates Don Eusebio's ritual (8 months ago), and is often the first plot-hole question investigators raise. The answer is that the pit has *always* been there — Padre Saens, working alone after the rest of the Jesuit mission was gone, attempted a closing in 1763 and managed only a *partial* binding. He laid himself on the geometry as the center; the binding consumed his body (see C5). What he bought was time, not closure. The lineage of Antu-Rayo (carried by Kuyen's grandmother and, in this region, by Rosa's elders) maintained that partial seal with regular counter-rites for nearly six decades. As the lineage thinned out — elders dying without successors, families displaced by the *campañas al desierto* — the seal weakened on its own. San Ruiz was built on land that never should have been farmed, and its inhabitants suffered increasing manifestations (sleepwalking, livestock deaths, the Luz Mala) for years before the evacuation. Don Eusebio's ritual did not *open* the pit — it *widened* a wound that had been slowly opening on its own. When Rosa's community left, they knew the danger was rising; they did not know yet that a neighbor was about to pry it open the rest of the way. Rosa can convey this if pressed.
- There are marks on the *inside* of several doorframes — the same angular scratched symbols from the chapel, in miniature. Some families were trying to protect their homes.
- The symbols on the doorframes are the counter-symbol (the binding), not the opening diagram from Don Eusebio's pit. Even here, someone was fighting back.
- If investigators examine the bread: **Natural History or Chemistry** — the bread is not molded, despite being at least a year old. The air in San Ruiz is drier than it should be. Something about the land here resists organic process.

**Available Clues in the Village**:
| Location | Clue | Skill |
|---|---|---|
| Doorframes | Scratched binding symbols — multiple houses | Spot Hidden |
| Kitchen table | Preserved bread — unnatural lack of decay | Natural History / Chemistry |
| Main road | Two different shoe/foot types — departure was group, mixed ages, calm | Tracking |
| One house (northeast) | A child's drawing on the wall: a circle with lines and a stick figure standing outside it | Spot Hidden |
| The well | The water tastes faintly of minerals — same metallic note as the pit | Taste / Chemistry |

---

## NPC: ROSA

**Role**: The last witness. The keeper of what happened. A partial guide to truth.

**Appearance**: 71 years old. Mapuche-Tehuelche descent, short, wide-built, with a face like carved ironwood — deep lines, dark eyes that have looked at the world steadily for a long time. She wears a black dress, a wool shawl despite the heat, and a small silver ornament at her throat that is not quite a cross — four lines meeting at angles. Her hands are always busy: she is usually mending, grinding, or weaving. She works while she talks.

> **Visual handout**: see `assets/binding-symbol.svg`. This is the silver ornament at Rosa's throat. The same symbol is scratched on the inside of doorframes in San Ruiz, on the reverse of Tomás's vizcachera stone (C1), and — inside-out — on the wax seal of the folded parchment Mercedes hands the players in C11. It is the inverse of the dual diagram's outward radiation. Print small; use as a prop.

![The binding symbol — Rosa's silver ornament](assets/binding-symbol.svg)

**Voice**: Low, measured. She does not hurry. She will wait through silences that make others uncomfortable. She speaks in a mix of Spanish and occasional Mapudungun words she does not translate — not to be obscure, but because some things, she says, do not exist in Spanish.

**Where She Is Found**: In the last house at the east end of the village, closest to the chapel. The door is open. She is grinding corn. She does not appear surprised to see strangers. *"Ya pensaba yo que iba a venir alguien tarde o temprano,"* she says, without looking up. *"Siéntense."* — *"I thought someone would come eventually. Sit down."*

When the investigators sit, before any question is asked, Rosa looks up at them for the first time. She studies them for perhaps five seconds. Then:

> *"Estuvieron en el pozo. Lo huelo. Cargan el polvo encima."*  — *"You've been at the pit. I can smell it on you. You carry the dust on you."*

She returns to her grinding. **This is the campaign's first naming of the dust runner** (see `flowmap.md`). The dust from Don Eusebio's burial pit settles on clothing and does not wash out. Rosa can smell it — minerality, a dry edge under the wool. She will not explain how she knows. The investigators *do* carry it; their saddlebags, their boots, their hat-bands. Other Marked-adjacent NPCs will notice across the campaign. Do not mention this aloud after Rosa names it; let the recognitions accumulate as ambient. **See `assets/geometric-perception-cues.md` for the per-chapter dust callbacks.**

**Why She Stayed**:
> *"Alguien tiene que acordarse. Si yo me voy, es como si nunca hubiera pasado. La tierra olvida más rápido que la gente."* — *"Someone needs to remember. If I leave, it is as if it never happened. The land forgets faster than people do."*

She stayed also because she is too old to be afraid of what might come back, and because she believes — correctly — that her presence near the chapel's symbols helps maintain the partial binding she and others scratched there before leaving.

**Motivation**: To be heard, finally. To pass what she knows to someone who might act on it correctly. She does not trust easily, but she is not hostile. She is *tired*. The investigators are possibly the first people she has spoken to in months.

---

**Possible Questions & Answers — Rosa**

*"Where did everyone go?"*
> *"Lejos. Al sur, los más. A Tres Lagunas, donde la familia. Unos al este, donde la tribu."* *(She means Kuyen's people.)* *"Se fueron antes que se pusiera peor. Yo les dije que se fueran antes."* — *"Away. South, most of them. To Tres Lagunas, to family. Some east, to the tribe. They went before it got worse. I told them to go sooner."* *(She resumes grinding.)*

*"Why did they leave? What happened here?"*
> *"Empezó como sueños. El mismo sueño, en muchos — un lugar luminoso debajo de la tierra, algo que tiraba para arriba. Después los animales. Después los chicos dejaron de dormir."* *(Pausa.)* *"Después la gente empezó a irse de noche al campo del sur. No corriendo — caminando. Con calma. Como si los hubieran invitado."* *(Deja de moler.)* *"Se fueron tres. Volvieron dos, mal. Uno no volvió."* — *"It started as dreams. The same dream, many people — a bright place underground, something pulling upward. Then the animals. Then the children stopped sleeping. Then people started going to the south pasture at night. Not running — walking. Calm. Like they were invited. Three went. Two came back wrong. One didn't come back."*

*"What do you mean, 'came back wrong'?"*
> *"Se sentaban. Comían. Contestaban preguntas. Pero ya no miraban a uno como antes. Como mirar el retrato de una persona en lugar de la persona."* *(Toca el adorno de plata que tiene al cuello.)* *"Los mandamos al sur con los otros. No sé qué son ahora."* — *"They sat. They ate. They answered questions. But they didn't look at you the same way anymore. Like looking at a painting of a person instead of a person. We sent them south with the others. I don't know what they are now."*

*"Who is responsible for this?"*
> *"La tierra no se lo hizo sola. Alguien llamó."* *(Los mira de frente por primera vez.)* *"Alguien dibujó la figura. La figura llama al ser. El ser contesta."* — *"The land didn't do this by itself. Someone called. Someone drew the shape. The shape calls the thing. The thing answers."* *(She will not say Don Eusebio's name. Not because she doesn't know — she may — but because naming the guilty is not her role here. Finding the shape is.)*

*"What are the marks on the doorframes?"*
> *"Defensas. Mapuche viejo, tehuelche viejo, mezclado — no siempre nos pusimos de acuerdo en las palabras, pero sí en la necesidad."* *(Pausa.)* *"No alcanzó. La figura estaba ya demasiado completa. Como tratar de tapar un río con las manos después de la lluvia."* — *"Warding. Old Mapuche, old Tehuelche mixed — we didn't always agree on the words but we agreed on the need. Not enough. The shape was too complete by then. Like trying to dam a river with your hands after the rain."*

*"What is in the chapel?"*
> *(Se queda quieta un momento.)* *"Lo que había en la capilla."* *(Vuelve a su trabajo.)* *"Vayan a ver. Pero vayan de día. Y no — sea lo que sea lo que oigan ahí, no le contesten. Ella no les habla a ustedes."* — *"What was in the chapel. Go see. But go during the day. And don't — whatever you hear there, don't answer it. She's not speaking to you."*

*"Who is 'she'?"*
> *"Dolores. Vivía acá. Entendió lo que estaba pasando antes que ninguno de nosotros."* *(Pausa.)* *"Trató de pararlo sola. Pueden ver lo que rascó encima de los símbolos viejos. Trabajó tres días. Después ella..."* *(Rosa no termina. Mira la puerta, en dirección a la capilla.)* *"Vayan a ver."* — *"Dolores. She lived here. She understood what was happening before any of us. She tried to stop it alone. You can see what she scratched over the old symbols. She worked for three days. Then she... Go see."*

*"Why is the chapel burned?"*
> *(She does not look up.)* *"Lo quemaron la noche que Dolores murió. Para que no terminara. Las paredes aguantaron."* — *"They burned it the night Dolores died. To stop her finishing. The walls held."* *(She grinds for a long moment, then adds, quietly:)* *"Eran dos. Hombres que conocía hacía cuarenta años. Entraron a la capilla con kerosén como quien camina a buscar agua. No hablaron. No corrieron cuando se les vino el techo encima. Lo que quedó de ellos lo sacamos a la mañana siguiente. Tenían la misma cara que los que se iban al sur de noche. La figura ya los tenía."* — *"Two of them. Men I'd known forty years. They walked into the chapel with kerosene the way you walk to fetch water. They didn't speak. They didn't run when the roof came down on them. We pulled what was left of them out the next morning. They had the same look on their faces as the ones who'd been going south at night. The shape had them already."*

> *(She lifts the silver ornament at her throat — the four-line cross — and turns it once between her fingers.)* *"Ahí entendí que la figura no solamente mata. Usa."* — *"That's when I understood the shape doesn't only kill. It uses."*

*"Are the tribes responsible for the cattle deaths?"*
> *(A long silence. Then:)* *"Eso se los dijo el Valdez."* *(It is not a question.)* *"No. La gente de la Kuyen viene tratando de cerrar lo que él abrió. Vienen haciendo el cierre desde antes de que empezaran a morirse los animales."* *(She sets down her grinding stone.)* *"A ustedes les mintieron."* — *"The Valdez man told you that. No. Kuyen's people have been trying to close what he opened. They've been conducting the binding since before the cattle started dying. You've been lied to."*

*"What should we do?"*
> *(She does not look up.)* *"Soy una vieja moliendo maíz. Yo no le digo a los hombres con fusiles qué tienen que hacer. Les digo lo que sé. Lo que sé es esto: la cosa a la que llamaron todavía no está acá del todo. Los rezos — el de la Kuyen, el de la Dolores, los de los marcos de las puertas — eso es lo que la mantiene al borde. Hagan lo que hagan, háganlo sabiendo eso. Si el cierre se rompe antes de terminarse, pasa adentro. Y después no hay nada entre ello y todo lo demás."* *(She returns to her grinding.)* *"Ustedes vinieron por el patrón. Yo no soy el patrón. Decidan a qué vinieron a ser."* — *"I'm an old woman grinding corn. I don't tell men with rifles what to do. I'll tell you what I know. What I know is this: the thing that was called is not yet fully here. The rituals — Kuyen's, Dolores's, the doorframes — those are what's keeping it at the edge. Whatever you decide to do, do it knowing that. If the binding breaks before it is finished, it comes through. And then there is nothing between it and everything. You came here for the patrón. I am not the patrón. Decide what you came here to be."*

> **Keeper note (D2)**: Rosa intentionally does not say *"go find Kuyen and let her finish."* She gives the players the *stakes* (binding incomplete = entity through; rituals are doing real work) and lets them work the rest out. A Marked player at this table can read the binding shape on Rosa's doorframe and on her ornament and connect it to the chapel's scratched layer; that is the player solving, not Rosa solving for them. If players are completely stuck after this conversation, fall back to the chapel encounter and La Llorona, where the *dead* speak more directly than the living.

**Roleplaying Hook**: Rosa will not give all of this information in one sitting. The first meeting she gives the essentials: people left, something was called, the chapel matters. If investigators ask respectfully and listen — actually listen, do not rush — she gives more. If they dismiss her or treat her as superstitious, she gives them the minimum and sends them to the chapel.

**Rosa's Hidden Knowledge**: She knows the complete binding symbol. She scratched it from memory on the floor beneath her corn-grinding stone. She will share it only if investigators have proven themselves trustworthy — likely only if they survive the chapel encounter and return to her.

---

## SCENE 2 — THE CHAPEL OF SAN RUIZ

### Setting Description

> *La capilla se alza en el extremo este del camino del pueblo, casi con la espalda contra la cerca vieja. Era chica desde el principio — cuatro paredes, un techo de madera que se vino abajo a la mitad en el incendio, un solo dintel arqueado todavía en pie. El fuego pegó fuerte; las paredes están tiznadas de negro en franjas sobre las ventanas. La cruz de madera sobre la puerta es ceniza. Pero las paredes de piedra están enteras, y están cubiertas.*
>
> *En cada superficie interior — dos capas. Primero, talladas en la piedra: líneas profundas, limpias, geométricas y precisas, que tejen iconografía católica (cruces, formas de pez) con dibujos angulares mapuche. Son viejas. El tallado pidió manos hábiles y tiempo. Esto fue obra de toda una comunidad.*
>
> *Por encima de ellas — rascadas sobre el hollín y el revoque, apuradas, casi frenéticas, con algo afilado — un segundo juego de trazos. La misma geometría, pero al revés. Invertida. Donde los símbolos tallados se abren hacia afuera, los rascados se cierran hacia adentro. Donde uno abre, el otro sella.*

> **Visual handout**: the carved layer is the *opening* aspect of the dual diagram (`assets/dual-diagram.svg`). The scratched layer is Dolores's counter-binding work in miniature — the same shape as Rosa's silver ornament (`assets/binding-symbol.svg`). Show both at the table when the players enter the chapel; their relationship as one geometry is the chapter's central revelation, and showing carries it where describing does not.

**Keeper Notes**:
- The carved symbols (original) are the *opening diagram* — the same geometry as Don Eusebio's pit, rendered in devotional form. The community had been incorporating it into their religious practice for years, unknowingly reinforcing it. A **Cthulhu Mythos or Occult (Hard)** roll: this pattern predates the chapel. It was here before the building. The community built the chapel *on* it.
- The scratched symbols (counter) are Dolores's work. She recognized the opening diagram for what it was and spent three days inverting every symbol she could reach. Her work is imperfect — she ran out of time — but it disrupted the pattern enough to slow the acceleration. These are the binding symbols, the same ones on Rosa's doorframes, on Tomás's stone (reverse side, if players examine it carefully).
- A **Spot Hidden** in the corner behind the collapsed altar: Dolores's tool. A sharpened piece of iron gate railing, worn smooth at the grip end from hours of use. On its flat side, scratched in tiny letters: *"no alcancé la mitad"* — "I didn't finish half."
- **The fire** (Keeper context, see Rosa's account): The chapel was burned the night Dolores died, by two villagers who walked in with kerosene under the same compulsion that pulls people to the south pasture at night. Both died in the collapse. The pattern *uses* people; this is the first time the players see it deploy a person as a weapon. The walls held — the stone-carved opening diagram is intact; only the wooden roof and Dolores's life were lost. **Players who note the soot pattern around the doorway** (Spot Hidden) see two sets of footprints leading *in* and none leading *out*.

**SAN Check**: 0/1 — the chapel itself, the weight of what it represents, the two layers of symbols telling a story of attempted salvation.

> **[THIS TABLE — 2026-05-24] INNER WALLS ENTIRELY BROKEN. SEAL DESTROYED.** The players broke the inner walls. Dolores's counter-symbols are rubble. The clay binding symbol beneath the floor is intact but buried. Rosa's prayer has no surface to anchor. La Llorona is displaced and enraged — eyes open, moving east toward the pit. The Zonda arrived early as a direct consequence. Full cascade: `TABLE-STATE.md`.

---

### Examining the Symbols

**Skill checks and what they reveal**:

| Skill | Result |
|---|---|
| Occult | The carved symbols are ritual geometry — their purpose is to draw something toward a fixed point. The scratched symbols attempt to reverse this. The conflict between them creates interference — it weakened the original but didn't stop it. |
| Art/Craft (Drawing) or Architecture | The carved symbols are extremely precise. The spacing and angles are mathematically consistent. The scratched symbols are approximate — the work of someone who understood the *intention* but was working from memory and instinct, not training. |
| History | The carved foundation symbols are older than the chapel's construction (the chapel went up perhaps 25 years ago, after independence). They might be colonial-era. Or older. Much older. |
| Library Use (against recovered documents) | If investigators have the manuscript fragment (acquired later from Don Eusebio's study), the carved symbols match its diagrams exactly. |
| Cthulhu Mythos | The geometry is not religious. It is dimensional. The opening diagram creates a sustained weakness in spatial geometry — a path. The binding closes the path. Both the Mapuche patterning and the Catholic iconography are overlay — the core symbol is something neither tradition created. |

**The Fragment**: In the rubble beneath the collapsed roofing, investigators with **Spot Hidden** find a piece of carved stone — broken from the wall, presumably in the fire or collapse. It shows a segment of the opening diagram combined with a partial binding overlay. Together with the hide and Tomás's stone, this is the third and most complete fragment. A player who has all three and makes an **INT** roll can now visualize roughly 75% of the complete diagram. The geometry is almost familiar. Like a shape seen in a dream.

---

## SCENE 3 — LA LLORONA

### The Entity: La Llorona

**What she is (for the Keeper only)**: La Llorona — The Weeping Woman — is one of Latin America's oldest and most persistent folkloric figures: a woman who lost her children (usually by her own hand in the original legend) and now wanders, weeping, searching. In your game, she is neither demon nor angel. She is a *remnant* — the psychic echo of **Dolores Quiroga**, a woman of San Ruiz who understood what was happening, acted with total commitment, and failed, and whose grief and determination left an impression in the ritual-charged space of the chapel so strong that something of her remained.

She is not conscious in a full human sense. She is an echo playing on repeat. She moves between the symbols she scratched, touching them, checking them, weeping. Occasionally a fragment of her original awareness surfaces — and in those moments, she can speak. What she says is not addressed to anyone in particular. It is what she was thinking when she died.

**Appearance**: A woman in her 40s, in a dark dress, dark hair loose. She is translucent — not invisible, but thin, like a figure seen through smoke. Her face, when visible, is not frightening. It is exhausted. Her eyes are closed most of the time. Her hands move constantly, touching the scratched symbols on the walls, checking each one.

**Sound**: Low, continuous weeping — not the theatrical wail of folklore but quiet, private weeping. The sound someone makes when they have been crying for a long time and the sound has become almost involuntary. Occasionally words are audible, in Spanish, half-whispered.

**Movement**: She moves between the scratched symbols in sequence, in the same order, always. She is checking her work. Every 3–4 minutes she pauses at the place where her tool ran out of reach (the high sections of the far wall) and her weeping intensifies briefly. Then continues.

**Behavior Sequence**:

1. **Entrance**: As investigators examine the symbols, the temperature drops noticeably — 4–5°C. The sound of weeping becomes audible before she is visible.
2. **Manifestation**: She appears at the far end of the chapel near the original carved altar location, moving toward the first scratched symbol.
3. **Ignoring the investigators**: She does not acknowledge them. She moves between her symbols. She is not performing for an audience.
4. **Moments of partial awareness**: At certain symbols — the ones she scratched with most urgency — she pauses, and speaks. These are not responses to questions. They are fragments of her last conscious moments:

> *"No me escucharon. Les mostré las figuras y me dijeron que yo estaba confundida. Las mujeres siempre estamos confundidas."* — *"They didn't listen. I showed them the shapes and they said I was confused. Women are always confused."*

> *"El Valdez — lo vi en el campo. Vi lo que estaba haciendo. No sabía lo que estaba haciendo. Esa es la peor clase."* — *"The Valdez man — I saw him in the field. I saw what he was doing. He didn't know what he was doing. That is the worst kind."*

> *"Llegaron tarde. Ya estaban tarde antes de llegar. Pero eso no quiere decir que paren."* — *"You're too late. You were too late before you arrived. But that doesn't mean you stop."*

> *"Busquen a la Kuyen. Ella sabe el cierre entero. Díganle — díganle que la pared del este está sin terminar. Yo no llegué."* — *"Find Kuyen. She knows the full binding. Tell her — tell her the eastern wall is incomplete. I couldn't reach."*

5. **Reaction to the stone fragment**: If investigators place the carved stone fragment on the ground near her path, she stops. Kneels (or approximates kneeling — she doesn't quite interact with physical surfaces consistently). She touches the fragment. She says: *"Sí. Sí, ésta es la parte a la que no llegué. Llévensela. Llévensela a la Kuyen."* — *"Yes. Yes, this is the part I couldn't reach. Take it. Take it to Kuyen."* Then resumes her circuit.

6. **If provoked/touched**: If an investigator attempts to touch her, pass through her, or interact physically — she does not harm them. But the investigator feels a rush of emotion that is not theirs: exhaustion, determination, grief, and beneath it, a terror so controlled it has become almost calm. **SAN 1/1D6 if provoked**. The emotion fades within seconds.

7. **Hidden remains**: In the far corner, beneath the collapsed roof section and a fallen beam — visible only if investigators move the debris (STR roll or combined effort) — a shallow depression in the earth floor. In it: small bones. A child's, probably. And beside them, scratched into the clay below the floor, the binding symbol in its *complete* form, drawn with a finger in the dirt by someone who knew the end was coming and wanted to leave the answer where it might be found. **This is the key clue of Chapter 2.**

> **C3 redundancy (clue retrieval)**: La Llorona points to this corner *unambiguously*. Once during her circuit she will pause at the far corner above the buried bones and *kneel, weeping more quietly than she has anywhere else*. Her hands move across the floor in the air above the depression — touching nothing — as if checking that what is buried is still there. If the players have not yet noticed the depression, the GM should **read this beat aloud** and let the players draw the conclusion. *No roll required to notice her doing this.* This guarantees the key clue does not depend on a STR roll alone — the players have a second visual signpost from the dead woman herself, who knows exactly where she put it.

8. **Departure**: After approximately 10 minutes, she moves to the altar position — the center of her circuit — and fades. The temperature rises. The weeping stops. As she disappears, the ash on the floor briefly stirs into a circular shape — the same geometry — and settles.

**SAN Check**: 0/1D4 (sustained presence and weeping)

---

### Optional: The Child's Remains

The child's bones are small — approximately 4–6 years old. They are arranged with care. There is a small carved wooden animal (a horse or guanaco) beside them. There is no sign of violence. The child was placed here deliberately, in protection.

**If investigators investigate**: A **Medicine** roll — the child did not die violently. Likely illness or exposure. The burial is recent enough (within two years) to have occurred after the ritual disturbances began. Someone — Dolores, probably — chose this place as a last safe location for a child who died during the crisis.

**SAN Check** (if investigators examine): 0/1D3 — not horror, but sorrow.

**Roleplaying hook**: If an investigator has children, or has lost a child, the Keeper should note this scene quietly. No mechanical penalty — just a moment of human weight. The horror of this arc is not just cosmic. It is about what people do to protect the ones they love, and how often it isn't enough.

---

## END OF CHAPTER 2

### Rosa's silent prayer (atmospheric runner — the prayers, 4)

After the investigators leave San Ruiz — when their horses are out of sight on the road east — Rosa walks alone to the burned chapel. She kneels at the depression in the floor, where Dolores buried her child and her own clay-finger record of the binding. She places her hands on the earth. She says nothing aloud.

> **What she is praying** (GM only — never told to players, never explained):
>
> *Por las que vinieron antes y por las que vendrán después.*  — *"For those who came before, and for those who come after."*
>
> Six words. Her own composition. She has been saying them daily for fourteen months. **It is what is sustaining the partial binding** in the chapel walls, alongside the scratched symbols. Without Rosa, the chapel would have failed entirely a year ago.

She kneels for sixty seconds. She gets up. She goes back to her grinding stone. The chapel walls hold for another month.

This is the campaign's third named prayer (see `flowmap.md`, *The Three Named Prayers*). It is **silent**. Players will not hear it. **It is what folk practice as functional ritual looks like**: not magical, not Mapuche, not Catholic, just consistent. The geometry recognizes consistency. If players ever return to San Ruiz alive — in C8 on the ride east, or in the C12 epilogue — Rosa is still there, still saying it daily. A Marked PC who lingers at the chapel doorway in any future scene will feel the prayer as a **felt geometry**, not as words.

---

**The key clue recovered**: The complete binding symbol — drawn by Dolores in the clay beneath the floor. With this, investigators (or Kuyen) have everything needed to complete the ritual.

**What players should now believe or know**:
- Don Eusebio opened this. Not the tribes.
- The tribes — specifically Kuyen's people — have been performing counter-rituals to close it.
- Dolores understood and tried to help. She failed alone.
- The binding symbol exists in complete form and can be used.
- Something is still incomplete — "the eastern wall."

**What players should NOT yet know**:
- What the entity actually is or looks like.
- That Nahuel is cracking under the strain.
- That Don Eusebio knows the investigators are getting close and is considering more drastic action.

---

## GM NOTES

**The emotional core**: This chapter is about grief and the tragedy of being right too late. Dolores knew. Rosa knew. The village was warned. Nothing was enough. Let the players feel the weight of that. Don't rush it.

**Empathy, not terror**: La Llorona should not be frightening. She should be heartbreaking. If players leave this scene unnerved by her sadness rather than her scariness, you have done your job. The horror comes later — from knowing that someone tried this hard and it still wasn't enough.

**Doubt before Chapter 3**: By the end of this chapter, investigators should be doubting everything Don Eusebio told them and beginning to feel the first edges of guilt — they were hired to stop the tribes, who are the only people actually helping. If they have reported back to Don Eusebio at any point and given him information about Kuyen's location, they should now realize they may have done something terrible.

**Rosa's final word**: If investigators return to Rosa after the chapel encounter, she will look at them without warmth but without hostility. *"Ahora ya saben en qué están metidos."* — *"Now you know what you're in the middle of."* If asked about the binding, she will draw the complete symbol from beneath her grinding stone and place it in front of them — silently, then resume work. She does not name what to do next. *"Ustedes saben más que yo ahora,"* she says — *"You know more than I do now."* (Marked players, looking at the shape, *do*.)

### Observable consequences (D5) — what the world *does*, not what NPCs say

Use these in passing, without explanation. They are the chapter's silent argument that geometry is real.

- **At Rosa's doorway**: Dust drifts in the morning wind, but at the doorway it stops *exactly* at the threshold — not pushed by the door, not blocked by the doorframe. It simply does not pass. The doorframe binding works. Marked players see the ornament-shape in the dust pattern itself.
- **At a doorframe whose binding has cracked**: Dust drifts in. A bird flies past and *flinches* halfway through the passage, banking sharply. The binding has begun to fail.
- **In the chapel during La Llorona's manifestation**: The temperature drop is measured (4–5°C, already in the prep). Add: a candle the players bring in *bends toward the eastern wall* — the wall Dolores could not finish. The flame leans about 15°. There is no draft.
- **When the players carry the stone fragment out of the chapel toward Rosa**: Their compasses (if they have any — military issue, surveyor's tools) rotate slowly. By the time they reach Rosa's house, their compasses point *south*, not north. They will be wrong by 15° for about an hour, then correct themselves.

**None of this requires a roll.** It is description. The Marked player feels *why*; the unmarked player sees *that*.

**Don Eusebio's move**: If investigators have been in contact with him, he is beginning to suspect they are no longer working toward his goal. He may send a rider — one of his hands, loyal out of debt, not knowledge — to intercept them before they reach the tribe. The rider's job is to bring them back for a "meeting." This is optional pressure, not a combat encounter. The rider doesn't know why he was sent. He just works there.

---

## CLUES CARRIED FORWARD

| Object/Knowledge | Details |
|---|---|
| Complete binding symbol (clay drawing) | The full counter-ritual geometry |
| Stone fragment from chapel | Third piece of the opening diagram — now also shows binding overlay |
| Dolores's tool | Physical testimony; "I didn't finish half" — the eastern wall is incomplete |
| Rosa's knowledge | People went willingly; two came back wrong; Kuyen's people are performing the binding |
| La Llorona's words | "Find Kuyen. Tell her the eastern wall is incomplete." / "The Valdez man — he didn't know what he was doing." |

---

> **[THIS TABLE — 2026-05-24] THE DEPARTURE FROM SAN RUIZ**
>
> *The canonical close (Rosa's silent prayer, the chapel walls holding) does not happen at this table. The walls are rubble. Run the following scene as the investigators prepare to leave. The Zonda is still blowing.*

### The storm breaks

The wind has been wrong since they arrived — hot, dry, northwest-origin, the kind that carries the mineral smell of something large and disturbed. It runs for a good hour after the chapel collapses. Then it stops.

Not dies down. **Stops.** One gust, then nothing. The silence after a Zonda is always sudden, but this is more total than it should be. The dust doesn't even settle naturally — it simply is no longer moving.

---

### Rosa exits

Her door opens.

She is the only person in San Ruiz who is not wet. Not damp — *dry*. The Zonda carried a scant rain before it arrived; everything and everyone in the village is coated in grit and damp. Rosa's threshold is dry. Water ended at the door as if stopped by glass.

She looks at the sky first. Then at the investigators. Then toward the chapel.

Her face is not frightened. It is the face of someone who has been waiting for something they hoped would not arrive, and it has arrived.

> *"¿Qué tocaron?"*

She says this before she has fully cleared her doorframe. Low, flat, not an accusation yet — a diagnostic question, the same register she used when naming the doorframe binding. She is reading the absence of something that was always going to be there.

No one needs to answer. She can see the chapel.

She starts moving. Not running — but fast, the deliberate speed of someone who has stopped caring whether they look frightened. Halfway to the chapel she breaks into a run. Her voice rises as she crosses the rubble line:

> *"¡Qué han hecho! ¡Asnos! ¡No saben lo que han hecho!"*

She reaches the broken wall and drops to her knees at the threshold. Not a collapse — she kneels deliberately, the way she does at her grinding stone or her doorframe. Her hands find the rubble on either side of where the door used to be. She is weeping, and it is the weeping of someone who has been holding something up alone for fourteen months and just felt it fail.

She does not explain. She does not look at the investigators. She is grieving, and she is reading the damage, and she cannot do both and speak at the same time.

**Let this breathe. Do not fill the silence.**

---

### La Llorona exits

Out of the ruined chapel wall — not through the doorway, through the wall itself, through the rubble, through the gap where the stones used to be — she emerges.

Not the Dolores they met inside: closed eyes, circuit-walker, echo on repeat. **Her eyes are open.**

She moves slowly. No circuit — she is not checking her marks. There are no marks left to check. She has the deliberate, groundless movement of someone who has been freed from something and does not yet know what to do with the freedom.

She passes through Rosa.

Not through Rosa as if Rosa isn't there — through her gently, the way a hand passes through water when it isn't grasping. For a moment they occupy the same space. Dolores's face — Dolores's echo of a face — is **close to Rosa's face from the inside**, and she is **smiling**. Not happy. Tender. The smile of someone who recognizes another person and is grateful for what they did, and sorry they failed, and does not have time to say either. The smile of a woman who has held something for fourteen months and is handing it off, whether anyone takes it or not.

Rosa does not react physically. But something in her stillness changes — the kneeling quality shifts. She has been touched by something and felt it.

La Llorona passes through and continues moving. East. Away from San Ruiz. Away from the chapel.

Then she turns and looks at the investigators.

---

### The rage

**SAN 1/1D6 — the full turn. Eyes open. Attention full and focused.**

She knows who broke the walls.

She does not scream. She moves toward the nearest investigator with the groundless inevitability of something that has stopped performing grief and started performing purpose. She passes through the first investigator she reaches.

**That investigator gets a flash — not a vision, not a dream — a fact delivered whole:**

> *Fuego. La capilla ardiendo — no desde afuera, desde los propios símbolos, el diagrama de apertura tallado con décadas de devoción prendiendo en lo que ella rascó encima. Está en el rincón con la espalda contra la pared y el aire está mal y el niño está en el rincón y no tiene tiempo y no terminó y la pared del este está—*[SPOT OCULTO/DIFÍCIL]

Then it's gone. The investigator is standing in the rubble of San Ruiz in the daylight.

**SAN 1/1D6 — not the horror of it. The intimacy of it. Being inside someone's last moment.**

The clue this plants: *the child is in the corner*. If the investigators did not find the bones and the clay symbol beneath the floor — if they broke the walls and left — La Llorona has just told them what they missed. Not with words. With memory.

La Llorona is already turning eastward again, moving away, picking up speed. Toward the pit. Toward the geometry she never finished.

---

### The goat

She is already there.

Not approaching — **standing at the edge of the rubble** between the investigators and the departing Llorona, facing east. No one saw her arrive. She was in the road a moment ago and now she is here, horns low, looking at the space La Llorona occupies the way a dog looks at a smell: not confused, not frightened, tracking.

The goat charges.

Not a warning headbutt — a full-body run, horns aimed at the approximate center of mass of something that has no center of mass. She hits La Llorona like hitting a cold room — and La Llorona **recoils**. Not metaphorically. The echo staggers. The shape of her grief-form disrupts, the way a reflection disrupts when the water moves. She makes a sound — not heard, felt, a frequency in the sternum — and her eastward movement becomes a lurch, uncontrolled, faster, like something that has been struck moving away from the blow.

In a few seconds she is past the edge of the village and gone.

The goat is standing still. Facing east. Looking at where La Llorona was.

Then she turns and looks at the investigators. baahhh.

**She has not bleated. She has not made a sound. Her sides are not heaving. There is no sweat. She looks at them with horizontal pupils that do not show excitement or effort or anything at all, and then she looks away — already facing the road east, the direction of the encampment, the direction they are about to ride.**

She is already where they're going. She has been for a while.

**SAN 0/1** — not for the entity. For the goat. For the specific category of wrong that it is to watch an animal do what weapons can't.

---

### After — the deal (if the gravely injured PC is at the threshold)

*Run this only if one investigator has a Major Wound and is actively losing ground — at 2 HP or below, or failing a CON check on the ride. If no one is at that threshold yet, hold this beat for the first time it applies.*

As the investigators are mounting up, the gravely injured PC goes to their horse. The goat is already there — standing beside the animal, close, looking at the wound.

The others are not yet there. Thirty seconds, maybe a minute. Just the two of them.

The goat approaches. She gets very close — close enough that the PC should feel breath. She has none. She lowers her head until her eyes are level with theirs.

The understanding arrives whole. Not a voice. Not words. A fact, the way a fact arrives when you are very cold or very tired: clear, simple, not negotiable in its terms.

"> *You live. You close the pit with your hands. That is all.*"

Not the soul. Not loyalty. Not service. A placement at an ending — they must be present when the ritual closes, and they must not obstruct it. What happens to them after is their own business.

**The choice — pure decision, no roll:**
- **Accept**: The wound closes. Not healed — *closed*, as if it was never the kind of wound that kills. Something about them is different in a way no one can name. The goat, from this point, is never far from that PC specifically.
- **Refuse or don't respond**: The goat waits one beat, then steps back, and stands at her usual distance. The dying proceeds on whatever clock was already running. She does not react. She is already looking east.

The others arrive. The goat is in the road ahead of them. She is already where they're going.

---

*Leave San Ruiz before Rosa stands up. She will have something to say to them eventually, but it is not today, and today is not the right silence to fill.*

---

> **[THIS TABLE — C2 OUTCOME — 2026-05-24]**
>
> **Inner walls entirely broken. Seal destroyed.** The players broke the chapel walls entirely. Dolores's counter-symbols are rubble. Rosa's prayer has no surface to anchor to. The partial binding that held the entity at the edge for 14 months has failed. The entity is measurably closer to fully through.
>
> **The clay beneath the chapel floor** is still intact underground — buried under rubble, retrievable if someone goes back, but Rosa controls access and will not cooperate with these investigators. This is what the pit closing requires. It cannot be improvised.
>
> **La Llorona — enraged, displaced, moving east.** When her circuit was destroyed, a fragment of her original awareness surfaced. She is not destroyed — she is loose, without a pattern, with all her original grief and none of her exhausted calm. Her eyes are open. She is moving toward the burial pit, toward the geometry she never finished. She knows who broke the walls.
>
> **Zonda storm arrived early at San Ruiz.** Canonically the Zonda appears in C7 at the pit. Its arrival here, two arcs early, is a direct consequence of the chapel seal collapsing.
>
> **The goat — extracted, follows the party.** The players extracted the goat from the well. She now follows the party. She will precede them everywhere. She does not bleat, does not sweat, does not react to gunfire. She is Mandinga's creature, now visible to the entity's geometry for the first time since the gate opened. She is in play. See `assets/mandinga-sequence.md` for the deal mechanic.
>
> **Rosa** does not yet know the walls are gone — but she will, and when she does she will not cooperate with these investigators. Her ornament, her memory of the complete symbol, and access to the clay excavation all go through her. All closed until the relationship is repaired, if it can be.
| Child's remains | Emotional weight; someone sacrificed peace for protection |
